Here's what the search revealed:\n\n## Race Cache With Network (RCWN)\n\nThe RCWN feature in Necko adds the ability to race the cache with the network when the cache is slow. So if reading from the disk is slow, we will send a network request, and return the channel from the network, even though we have the entry in the cache.\n\n## Timing and Decision Logic\n\nIf the request is not using appcache, is smaller than 256 kb, and doesn't have alt-data, then if the cache is slow we race immediately, otherwise we set a timer for 3 * avgCacheTime.\n\n## Cache Queue and Racing\n\nThe racing algorithm is quite simple at this point: If racing is enabled, the request is allowed to hit the network, and the cache queue size is bigger than a certain threshold, then we trigger the network right before we query the cache.\n\n## Delay Issues\n\nThe search results also reveal that channels have been delayed by 20+ seconds just because of waiting for the cache to response.\n\n## Related Preferences\n\nOne way to control this behavior is to set the preference network.http.rcwn.max_wait_before_racing_ms to 0.\n\nThe search results primarily point to Mozilla Bugzilla discussions where developers have been working on optimizing the balance between cache access and network requests in the nsHttpChannel implementation.\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"parent_tool_use_id":"toolu_01MP23GjvKAmrQ35MG9E1yV1","session_id":"7a92fc91-110b-4eab-8fa4-1d191e6182af","uuid":"8a53a181-9d57-4111-b503-03f396d33ac7"}

if the cache queues are longer than a preset limit, a race is triggered before trying to find the cache entry.\n\nThe search results show various bug discussions and patches related to improving Firefox's handling of racing cache requests with network requests in the nsHttpChannel.cpp file.\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"parent_tool_use_id":"toolu_01MP23GjvKAmrQ35MG9E1yV1","session_id":"7a92fc91-110b-4eab-8fa4-1d191e6182af","uuid":"a5d4fbac-5062-481f-b19f-a5e9de01dea4"}

Here's what the search revealed:\n\n## Overview\n\nThe RCWN (Race Cache With Network) feature in Necko adds the ability to race the cache with the network when the cache is slow. If reading from the disk is slow, the browser will send a network request, and return the channel from the network, even though there is an entry in the cache, providing content to consumers faster.\n\n## How It Works\n\nFor requests that are not using appcache, are smaller than 256 kb, and don't have alt-data, the system races immediately if the cache is slow, or otherwise sets a timer for 3 times the average cache time.\n\nIf you visited a webpage in the past, usually most of the web page data is stored in cache on your disk. However, RCWN causes the browser to query the network again, even if cache data is available, if the disk does not respond fast enough, which causes additional data being consumed.\n\n## Implementation Details\n\nThe isRacing() method returns true if the channel raced the cache and network requests. In order to determine if the response is coming from the cache or the network, the consumer can check isFromCache(). The method can only be called after the channel fires its OnStartRequest notification.\n\n## Network Type Considerations\n\nThere is logic in place so that RCWN is not performed when the user is on a cellular network to avoid excess data usage.\n\nThe feature was landed in Firefox 57 and turned on in Firefox 59, with statistics showing that RCWN network wins in approximately 4% of requests.\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"parent_tool_use_id":"toolu_01MP23GjvKAmrQ35MG9E1yV1","session_id":"7a92fc91-110b-4eab-8fa4-1d191e6182af","uuid":"9d91aaa0-29b5-49aa-825e-1615ca94607e"}

And sometimes, even on a fast, unloaded PC with a blazing SSD, the network wins. https://t.co/pxB7DnANKV\\\" / X\",\"url\":\"https://x.com/ericlaw/status/1258095899215048713\"}]\n\nBased on the search results, here's what I found about \"MaybeRaceNetworkWithCache\" (also known as RCWN) in Firefox:\n\n## Overview\n\nFirefox introduced a feature called RCWN (Race Cache With Network) in 2017, which was intended to improve web performance by racing cached requests against the network.\n\n## How It Works\n\nFirefox implements a \"RCWN\" (race cache with network) strategy where it'll try to fetch assets that are already cached from the network when IO is slow on the device and re-issuing the network request will actually be faster than reading the file from disk. The RCWN feature in Necko adds the ability to race the cache with the network when the cache is slow. So if reading from the disk is slow, it will send a network request, and return the channel from the network, even though there is the entry in the cache. This way Firefox provides the content to consumers faster.\n\n## When It's Activated\n\nIf the request is not using appcache, is smaller than 256 kb, and doesn't have alt-data, then if the cache is slow, racing begins immediately, or otherwise a timer is set for 3 * avgCacheTime.\n\n## Concerns\n\nFirefox makes simultaneous requests against disk cache and network called \"Race Cache With Network\" (RCWN) which can cause issues in countries that don't offer unlimited data plans (mostly affects developing countries where data is expensive), as more data than necessary is consumed to display a web page.\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"parent_tool_use_id":"toolu_01MP23GjvKAmrQ35MG9E1yV1","session_id":"7a92fc91-110b-4eab-8fa4-1d191e6182af","uuid":"828f0316-bef5-467e-8793-0d3ad059fcba"}

If reading from the disk is slow, a network request will be sent, and the channel will return from the network, even though the entry exists in the cache.\n\n## How It Works\n\nThis feature changes the way the network cache works. When disk IO is detected as potentially slow, a network request is sent in parallel, and the first response that comes back is used. Firefox implements this \"RCWN\" strategy where it tries to fetch assets that are already cached from the network when IO is slow on the device, as re-issuing the network request will be faster than reading from disk.\n\n## Performance Benefits\n\nRCWN was a significant win on desktop, with desktop hard drives performing poorly often enough that racing the network resulted in real wins (10ms faster channel loads on average, with wins of multiple seconds for really slow cases).\n\n## nsHttpChannel Methods\n\nThe search results reference methods within `nsHttpChannel` related to racing:\n- nsHttpChannel::IsRacing is called from HttpChannelParent::OnStartRequest where it gets the value and sends it to the child process.\n\n## Configuration\n\nResources larger than 256kb are not raced because that's unlikely to improve performance, and racing only occurs when the disk cache is detected as very slow. RCWN can be disabled via about:config's \"network.http.rcwn.enabled\" setting.\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"parent_tool_use_id":"toolu_01MP23GjvKAmrQ35MG9E1yV1","session_id":"7a92fc91-110b-4eab-8fa4-1d191e6182af","uuid":"49583185-289c-4ddd-ae18-4388e85e3add"}
